  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText15561005802731840924" style="display:none"><i>The Brothers Grimm have a warning for the Land of Stories.</i><br /><br />Connor Bailey thinks his fairy-tale adventures are behind him - until he discovers a mysterious clue left by the famous Brothers Grimm. With help from his classmate Bree and the outlandish Mother Goose, Conner sets off on a mission across Europe to crack a two-hundred-year-old code.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Alex Bailey is training to become the next Fairy Godmother... but her attempts at granting wishes never go as planned. Will she ever be truly ready to lead the Fairy Council?<br /><br />When all signs point to disaster for the Land of Stories, Connor and Alex must join forces with their friends and enemies to save the day. But nothing can prepare them for the coming battle... or for the secret that will change the twins' lives forever.<br /><br />The third book in the bestselling Land of Stories series puts the twins to the test as they bring two worlds together!</span>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I don't think it was their father. I think it was their uncle. I'm betting their dad had a brother as it was mentioned in the book that he was the you<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I don't think it was their father. I think it was their uncle. I'm betting their dad had a brother as it was mentioned in the book that he was the youngest child which implies he had a sibling. Also, I'm betting that Emmerich is the masked man's (and Bo Peep's) son since he had to have magic blood to come through the portal and never knew his father.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

  <span id="freeText750749868292531720" style="display:none">Dear Mr. Colfer,<br /><br />I don't know if you reads these reviews, but this is the only way I could think of contacting you. I just finished reading book three in the Land of Stories series. I was quite pleased over all. Your humour with your characters continues to hold true. <br /><br />More importantly, however, I write because I would like to thank you for Alex's message to the Assembly on page 460, especially this portion, "They taught me that every creature is an individual and we can't punish an entire race for mistakes made by individuals. As easy as it is to label large groups with the reputations of their ancestors, it isn't right." Your message rings truth for their World and the Otherworld. Our world is so full of hate and judgement. As a teacher-librarian, I hope as my students read your novel they also see the message you and Alex have so clearly stated for the readers. <br /><br />Thank you again,<br />Lisa Price<br />Teacher Libraian,<br />Westwood Elementary, <br />Prince George, British Columbia, Canada </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer963229055" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6945428749128051835">OH MY GOSH! <br/><br/>That was brilliant. I loved every second of it. It was beyond awesome. I can't believe what I just read. <br/><br/>At first it was a but slow and I was like 'get to the point' but ad usual it was so worth it. <br/><br/>There are probably parts to this book I don't like but I don't remember them...   <span id="freeText6945428749128051835" style="display:none">OH MY GOSH! <br /><br />That was brilliant. I loved every second of it. It was beyond awesome. I can't believe what I just read. <br /><br />At first it was a but slow and I was like 'get to the point' but ad usual it was so worth it. <br /><br />There are probably parts to this book I don't like but I don't remember them... Well hated reading about the Grandè Armèe. It was terrible. <br /><br />And what I don't understand I that they said the masked man was in prison for a decade and I am pretty sure the twins dad has only be supposedly dead for three year. Though it was a very good surprise, bad for the twins, but brilliant for the book. I wonder what he is doing there? <br /><br />So because of the Grandè Armèe and the little glitch with the masked man I am giving the book 4.5 stars.<br /><br />I loved that the twins got love interests. It's so cute. Connor and Bree are so adorable. I wish they kissed. What Rook did was bad, but understandable, I hope things work out there, but I still would have loved if miraculously there was a prince she could be with, but that's just me being a girl and saying it's a fairytale...<br /><br />Oooh and I was so so so so so so so so so so so so so happy when Goldilocks tools Jack she was pregnant, it was the sweetest thing. <br /><br />I was quite sad when Sleeping Beauty couldn't have kids, but it was probably very realistic and I loved that. But everything worked out I the end and now they have Princess Ash. It's quite a beautiful unique name, I like it. It's modern, but still perfect to be a fairytale name. <br /><br />Trollbella is so cute. I love how she says <br /><br />“I tried to stay faithful to you for as long as I could and it was the hardest six days of my life. I was weak without you, Butterboy, and my heart strayed. I couldn’t bear the thought of being alone forever so I gave my heart to someone else.” <br /><br />It was adorable. So cute. She is dramatic and cute. Like how she tried to fight, and when the guy was dying and she just assumed he wanted to marry her, she doesn't really care about consent, does she? She just is free and happy. Also I love how the chapter ends with Connor saying <br /><br />“I just can’t believe Trollbella picked that troll over me.” <br /><br />It's like even though he never liked her he was still cocky about himself. He is the cutest 14 year old ever. <br /><br />I can't wait for the next book. It's going to be awesome!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6945428749128051835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I can connect his book to Percy Jackson because Percy is a demigod and he his very alike to the twins trying to fight creatures and also going on tasks. The only difference is that they are based on different generes.</span>

<div id="review_2794321864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794321864" />
    <a title="explorerofbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34290393-explorerofbooks"><img alt="explorerofbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559223817p2/34290393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2794321864?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="explorerofbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="explorerofbooks" href="/user/show/34290393-explorerofbooks">explorerofbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2794321864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2924343201249972617">“They taught me that every creature is an individual and we can’t punish an entire race for mistakes made by individuals. As easy as it is to label large groups with the reputations of their ancestors, it isn’t right.” Damn, this book hit a little too close to home. I’m so glad this is a children’s series filled with valuable lessons. Kids could learn a lot from this. <br/><br/>Connor and Alex are adapting to their new lives without each other. While Alex is becoming an excellent fairy-in-training, amateu</span>
  <span id="freeText2924343201249972617" style="display:none">“They taught me that every creature is an individual and we can’t punish an entire race for mistakes made by individuals. As easy as it is to label large groups with the reputations of their ancestors, it isn’t right.” Damn, this book hit a little too close to home. I’m so glad this is a children’s series filled with valuable lessons. Kids could learn a lot from this. <br /><br />Connor and Alex are adapting to their new lives without each other. While Alex is becoming an excellent fairy-in-training, amateur writer Connor is sent to Berlin to hear three newly discovered stories of the brothers Grimm. Trouble is arising, and a warning for the Land of Stories is clear in those new releases. Together with recently made friends, Connor has to travel around the world to solve the mystery and warn Alex. The twins will have to face their most dangerous enemy yet, combined with the most difficult thing to do: uniting everyone to defend their land. Meanwhile, the heroes will have to deal with heartbreak, loss and some hidden secrets coming out. Get ready to sit on the edge of your chair. <br /><br />My first point is, there were dragons! This is no spoiler, because it’s visible on the cover. DRAGONS! There even was a moment that had Daenarys vibes to it, and it left me squealing. Furthermore, this book dealt with serious issues, like death, racism, and infertility of women. These are all topics children should know more about. And about dragons, of course.<br /><br />There was a cliffhanger ending that made you crave the next book. I’m still here thinking about theories. The ending and other temporary ‘plot holes’ resulted in a logical build-up , making a sequel necessary. This is something the previous books didn’t,;they couldn’t have easily been standalones. Best part is, Colfer’s writing is also getting better. Or maybe it just didn’t bother me that much, since the plot was that exciting.<br /><br />We get more clues about the history of the Land of Stories, before the Queens lived. This showed Colfer is thinking more about world-building. Additionally, the past of our world was crucial to the story. Big names, like Napoleon and King Ludwig II of Bavaria (who was obsessed with castles) were mentioned. Does anyone want to go visit castle Neuschwanstein with me, because Colfer described it magically?<br />Where the set-up in the former books was always based on an object hunt, The Grimm Warning incorporated a puzzle to solve during a travel trip. It felt as if we were actually traveling along with Connor. There were so many plot twists that I didn’t see coming, and I just want to have the answers right now. The mysterious touch felt very refreshing, ex. villain’s identity, secret children, …<br /><br />Unfortunately, what irritated me in the first books happens many more times in The Grimm Warning. Everything happens because of coincidences. There were coincidences helping getting problems solved, but also making problems happen. This made things unrealistic, as if they never really had any obstacles to master.<br />Secondly, Connor’s friends, Bree and Emmerich, became a bit useless after 200 pages into the book. Although they were involved in a plot twist, I do would have loved to see them more involved into everything. The same goes for the princesses, who again got little identity. Also, I only realized now there’s a serious lack of diversity? You would think that a queer author, who was an actor in Glee, would think about some POC or queer characters. <br /><br />Nevertheless, The Grimm Warning is currently my favorite book in the series. 4 stars. There was actual tension, and some powerful lessons. Alex and Connor teach us that forgiveness and an open mind is necessary to have in our world. Colfer also knows what he’s talking about; it is clear he has delved into the subjects of folklore. He uses multiple minor unknown fairytales in comparison to Once Upon A Time, which simply started introducing Disney characters after a few seasons. If you’re into fairytales, prophecies and fantasy, feel free to check out these series. And maybe if your kids are looking for something to read, you could recommend this to them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2924343201249972617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Highly recommended for children and adults alike!</span>

  <span id="freeText3249543681093362889" style="display:none">I love this series, I really do. I think it's a great idea and a great concept, it's just so unfortunate that it isn't a great writer. I can't help but feel that the almost unanimous 5 stars it's due to it being Chris Colfer. But this book was ridiculous. And as I said previously, I love the whole idea of the series.<br /><br />It was hard for me to write this review but I was left so disappointed. <div id="review_1741780131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1741780131" />
    <a title="justonemorechapter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46660574-justonemorechapter"><img alt="justonemorechapter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451758027p2/46660574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1741780131?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="justonemorechapter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="justonemorechapter" href="/user/show/46660574-justonemorechapter">justonemorechapter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46660574-justonemorechapter?shelf=flat">flat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46660574-justonemorechapter?shelf=plot-twist-damn">plot-twist-damn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46660574-justonemorechapter?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46660574-justonemorechapter?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46660574-justonemorechapter?shelf=slow">slow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46660574-justonemorechapter?shelf=fantastic-series">fantastic-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1741780131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14908108121227277890">This review was originally posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.jutonemorechapter.ca'>www.jutonemorechapter.ca</a><br/><br/>I hate to say this, but A Grimm Warning was a let down. The first two books in this series were incredible- The stories moved quickly, they had an awesome concept, and they added extremely creative back story and depth to the Fairy tales we all thought we knew inside out. Unfortunately, when it came to this third installment things slowed down too much for my taste, and I felt I was just skimming the pages waiting for something interes</span>
  <span id="freeText14908108121227277890" style="display:none">This review was originally posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jutonemorechapter.ca">www.jutonemorechapter.ca</a><br /><br />I hate to say this, but A Grimm Warning was a let down. The first two books in this series were incredible- The stories moved quickly, they had an awesome concept, and they added extremely creative back story and depth to the Fairy tales we all thought we knew inside out. Unfortunately, when it came to this third installment things slowed down too much for my taste, and I felt I was just skimming the pages waiting for something interesting to happen. (A problem I never had for books one and two).<br /><br />For those of you who don’t know, Chris Colfer is most commonly known for playing Kurt Cobain in the very popular TV show, Glee. I’ve watched most of Glee, and Chris’s character is one of my favourites, so when I heard he was trying out novel writing I couldn’t wait to get my hands on his books. I was even happier to find out how creative a writer he is… however I found this series, The Grimm Warning in particular, was the most literarily advanced book.<br /><br />I have not gone to University and studied English, so it’s probably not my place to say someone’s writing isn’t that great, but the problem is, neither did Chris Colfer. He’s only gone to college for two weeks before dropping out to be in Glee (which obviously ended up being a great idea). I don’t mean to sound pretentious, but some parts of The Grimm Warning sounded like something a high school student came up with for creative writing in English. I never noticed that in the first two books, but I’m guessing that’s because of how absorbed I was by the actual storyline. Either way, The Land of Stories is meant for more of a younger audience, so I guess I shouldn’t be complaining.<br /><br />Like I mentioned previously, The Grimm Warning (and this series in general) is one of the most creative series I’ve come across. The first two blew my mind, but though the Grimm Warning had yet another amazing idea, there was too much waiting around, and development happened rarely and slowly. The whole concept of the Grimm Brother’s having written a story nobody had heard before had so much potential! Based off the other books, Chris Colfer could have done an amazing job with it. The problem was, a real-life historical figure was mixed in with the fairy tales, and I feel like it was just too much at once. There wasn’t enough action, and too much of awkwardly forcing two different things together.<br /><br />In the end, the INSANELY UNEXPECTED plot twist in the last pages of the book saved this series for me, as if it weren’t for that twist I definitely would not have gone on to read the next book in the series. I’m not going to spoil it for anybody, but I had absolutely no idea it would happen AT ALL. I hadn’t even considered that plot twist.<br /><br />In conclusion, The Grimm Brothers had a pretty flat plotline that made finishing it very difficult. There’s no way I’m not reading the next book after that plot twist, though. This series is a must-read for any 11-13 year old who likes the classic fairy tales.<br /><br />-R<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14908108121227277890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Katherine Tingen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59397939-katherine-tingen"><img alt="Katherine Tingen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2264151573?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine Tingen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine Tingen" href="/user/show/59397939-katherine-tingen">Katherine Tingen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264151573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9525218502695979858">“A Grimm Warning” by Chris Colfer is a adventurous tale where the reader is constantly caught in a whirlwind of fairy tales. Conner goes to Germany and hears a warning to tell his sister, Alex, that will help keep the fairytale world safe. When Alex hears that an army from France has just about entered into the fairytale world the kingdoms are in complete chaos. Alex and Conner travel far to unite the kingdoms and re-establish peace throughout the land. I really enjoyed reading the third book in</span>
  <span id="freeText9525218502695979858" style="display:none">“A Grimm Warning” by Chris Colfer is a adventurous tale where the reader is constantly caught in a whirlwind of fairy tales. Conner goes to Germany and hears a warning to tell his sister, Alex, that will help keep the fairytale world safe. When Alex hears that an army from France has just about entered into the fairytale world the kingdoms are in complete chaos. Alex and Conner travel far to unite the kingdoms and re-establish peace throughout the land. I really enjoyed reading the third book in the series “The Land Of Stories”. I thoroughly enjoyed “A Grimm Warning” because there wasn’t a time when things got boring. Chris Colfer kept the reader entertained with different features like romance, action, and fantasy. Although I loved the book there were a few things I disliked. One of which was when Colfer let you off the hook at cliffhangers. Some of the cliffhangers that were meant to draw the reader in and question things were either never mentioned again or could always be guessed about what was going to happen next before it happened; most of the time you were right. I think the theme of the book is that hard work can pay off in the end. I think this because the harder Alex and Conner worked, the faster they were able to achieve things, be rewarded, and do what they wanted. Hard work in the end will pay off. Maybe not now, or tomorrow, but someday it will.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15504197274074661619"> After book two, Connor and Alex Bailly are reunited once again in book three of Chris Colfers Land of Stories: A Grims Warring to fight the greater enemy, Napoleon's army. After two hundred years of being trapped in a portal by the Fairy God Mother, they must find a way to protect their homeland and defeat Napoleon's army. <br/><br/> This story The major theme that surfaced in the third book was friendship and coming together again. I believe this because because Connor uses his friends to help get throu</span>
  <span id="freeText15504197274074661619" style="display:none"> After book two, Connor and Alex Bailly are reunited once again in book three of Chris Colfers Land of Stories: A Grims Warring to fight the greater enemy, Napoleon's army. After two hundred years of being trapped in a portal by the Fairy God Mother, they must find a way to protect their homeland and defeat Napoleon's army. <br /><br /> This story The major theme that surfaced in the third book was friendship and coming together again. I believe this because because Connor uses his friends to help get through the portal through the german castle. While Alex gets help to defend land of stories with all the queens and kings of the land, At the same time they were both trying to find a way to reunited to defeat greater good. Colfer in this particular book used more telling than showing. His sentences were short, used easy words to understand, I believe that he was trying to show the readers how mature Connor and Alex had become since the second book. Both twins had a little bit romance relationship in this particular book . Although this books had some things that did not impress me <br /><br /> I recommend this magical book to readers who and who have a taste for a bit of action, romance ,and fantasy.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1940712966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1940712966" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1483724-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530654339p2/1483724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1940712966?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/1483724-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=all-fiction">all-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=written-by-famous-people">written-by-famous-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1483724-kate?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1940712966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8882157802111039809">This is a solid third book for a series, and better than a lot of third books out there. Was it as good as the first two? No. Some of that may have been the format (I opted for the audiobook this time around, and as much as I love Chris Colfer, he's not my favorite narrator. There were way too many characters in this book and the accents and voices just didn't work for me, but I digress). <br/><br/>This book was slow to start, and there was a lot of superfluous scenes at the beginning that didn't necessar</span>
  <span id="freeText8882157802111039809" style="display:none">This is a solid third book for a series, and better than a lot of third books out there. Was it as good as the first two? No. Some of that may have been the format (I opted for the audiobook this time around, and as much as I love Chris Colfer, he's not my favorite narrator. There were way too many characters in this book and the accents and voices just didn't work for me, but I digress). <br /><br />This book was slow to start, and there was a lot of superfluous scenes at the beginning that didn't necessarily need to be there, especially considering how involved the main plot lines were. Once the core action started, it held my attention, and I'm not usually one to like listening to fiction via audiobooks (except fake memoir fiction). The ending was a bit predictable, but a solid cliffhanger. I'm interested enough to eventually read the next in the series. It's been a few years since I read book two and only just picked up this one, so we'll see when I get to it. It's not something I'm dashing to read right away, but I am curious to find out what happens. (But alas, I'm also twice as old as the target demo for this book, so my opinion is probably not as relevant).</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Cv22v3G8IV8M5oTH8Vhl8V7rn1OYce/3v7J77wA15JEw299tyuLoN6vNMKYGrW8uiLR4m1b8YZDkzD1ezXYWCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6UVvGhdMN/PNrObdVBzSQi6V+ymy7EMnOaOJIdUaOhjTYwbIrBL+m2qHUryj6did+Moc4XxhzUBi3c+QGFnIgg==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer15981619337954082137">Chris Colfer is an Emmy-nominated and Golden Globe-winning actor best-known for his portrayal of Kurt Hummel on the FOX television series "Glee". <br/><br/>He is also a New York Times bestselling author whose books include the first three novels in the "Land of Stories" series ("The Wishing Spell", "The Enchantress Returns" and "A Grimm Warning") as well as "Struck By Lightning: The Carson Philips Journal" </span>
  <span id="freeText15981619337954082137" style="display:none">Chris Colfer is an Emmy-nominated and Golden Globe-winning actor best-known for his portrayal of Kurt Hummel on the FOX television series "Glee". <br /><br />He is also a New York Times bestselling author whose books include the first three novels in the "Land of Stories" series ("The Wishing Spell", "The Enchantress Returns" and "A Grimm Warning") as well as "Struck By Lightning: The Carson Philips Journal" which is a novelization based on the script he wrote for the film "Struck By Lighting" (Colfer also co-produced and starred in that movie).</span>
